  2. I have had a couple of Braun razors before this and they have lasted at least 5 year without fault. The rechargeable battery in both just stopped holding a charge. I like the cordless feature, so I upgraded after battery failure.<br /><br />Because of the quality of my other Braun razors and also the design, I chose another Braun to upgrade to. I have tried some other brands, with different cutting styles, in the past, and they just didn't cut as well as Braun razors.<br /><br />This razor is very similar to my older Braun 7526 razor(lasted about 7 years, before the battery died). There are four main differences though. First, this razor has a fancier and more elegant look to it. It has a nice silver exterior and a fancy LCD screen(I barely looked at it). Secondly, I noticed there are different shaped holes on the foil. Next, I didn't notice any difference in the speed or quality of cutting my beard, despite the supposed more advanced technology. Finally, this razor was about twice as much as what I paid for the Braun 7526, about 9 1/2 years ago.<br /><br />This razor broke twice in 2 1/2 years. The first time it broke, I couldn't get the foil, or any other foil, to clip into place. I sent it in to be fixed under warranty. They replaced the whole head. Yesterday, I was shaving and when I tried to turn the razor off, I was surprised to find the switch wouldn't turn off! It's out of warranty and I figured that it would probably cost me almost as much as a new razor to have it fixed. Therefore, I attempted to try and fix it myself. I took it apart to try to fix it, to no avail. It's too complex and has a lot of small parts. I don't think it is possible to fix, without replacing the switch or something.<br /><br />Save yourself some money and buy this. It almost identical to the 7526. [[ASIN:B00006L9CA Braun 7680 Syncro Pro Solo Shaver Refurbished]] There is no difference in the cutting quality, in my opinion, between the two. The cutter block is exactly the same. Maybe the newer tech Braun razors cut better, but I doubt it. I think I'll just get the refurbished 7680 that I linked to above. Maybe I'll think about buying another model Braun in the future, but my experience with this model has ruined my trust in Braun quality.<br /><br />I'm always looking for a better and faster electric razor and willing to pay for it. I once spent over $300 for a Grundig razor out of the Sharper Image catalog, back around 1996. It broke soon after I got it. I don't think there has been significant improvement in cutting quality of electric razors in the past decade or more. There's a lot of hype and marketing for the newer razors, but it seems that they aren't any better.

  5. I've owned Braun electric shavers for almost 20 years now and have been happy with every one - until this one. The Series 5 has really been a let-down for me. I've had it now for 10 months. 1) Most importantly it just does not shave as well as my prior Braun's. I used to be able to shave once every other day with no issues at all. But with this Braun if I skip a day it's a painful undertaking complete with annoying pulls and even cuts. My previous Braun shavers never had issues getting to though spots but this one flat out can't get these (such as the neck line). Even after a shave with the Series 5 I don't feel smooth. 2) The station is set up so that if you want to charge, you have to use the cleaner. This is a way for them to ensure that you keep having to buy cleaning cartridges through the life of the razor. This is annoying and a blatant money grab from Braun - especially considering my previous Braun had the option to charge but not clean. Note that with the Series 5 you CAN charge but not clean, but you'll need to pull out the cleaning cartridge to do so - a needless hassle. Overall I am very disappointed with this razor and growing impatient with Braun and their attempt to force us to use their cleaning cartridges.
  6. The Braun Syncro System shavers debuted in the US around the spring of 2000 with the 7000 series. They made quite a splash, looking quite different from the predecessor, the Braun Flex Integral (6000 series). I bought the 7526 model and used it for about 4 years before moving up to the 8000 Activator series. The model I actually have is the 8595. The 8995 is essentially the same model, only renamed with a different model convention (now 5 series instead of Activator system 8000 series).<br /><br />If you can find the 8595 Activator for less money, get it instead of the 5 series 8995. The differences from the 8995 are only cosmetic, and minor at that.<br /><br />MODELS<br />The Braun 5 Series line consists of several models: 8975, 8985, and 8995. The top of the line is, naturally, the 8995. I suggest you go to [...] to see the spec comparison, as this site does a good job of showing you the differences. In a nutshell, they ALL have the same motor and cut exactly the same. The differences are in the number of indicators (the 8995 has an LCD screen, while the 8575 and 8585 use LED lights), some additional chrome trim, and the inclusion of the cleaning system (the 8575 does not have it).<br /><br />LCD INDICATOR<br />I chose the 8995(8595), because I wanted to have the LCD indicator (my prior model--the 7526--did not have one). The 8995 LCD will show you exactly how much charge you have left, how many minutes until fully charged, how many shaves your shaver has performed, and how many minutes you've spent shaving. Do you really need to know all this? Not really.<br /><br />The LCD will also tell you how many shaves you've done. It makes a count after about 1 minute from shut-off. So, if you shut off the unit for a moment to do something then go back to shaving a minute later, your counter will now have 2 shaves logged. It's not very useful information. What Braun should really do with the LCD is display a total hours operated counter and then show a warning for changing the foil/cutter once 12 months has been reached (you'd then have the option to reset the warning). I don't care how many shaves I've taken! Incidentally, the new 5 series model that replaces the 8995 has done away with the LCD (Braun went back to using just LED indicators--cheaper and they probably realized the LCD is not all that useful anyway).<br /><br />CHARGING<br />The unit fully charges in about an hour. That's quick. And once charged, it goes into a trickle charge mode so there's no danger of overcharging. The voltage control mechanism is very sophisticated and can take a wide range of voltages, worldwide. Braun perfected these electronics over several decades, so it has to be good. With models lacking an LCD, a red light will start to flash when the shaver charge is getting low. At that point, you've got about two shaves left. That's not bad. So, in essence, once it starts flashing you plug it in after your shaving is done. A full charge should last about 10 shaves. Compared to other shavers, this is quite competitive, especially given that it takes only 60 minutes to become fully charged. If you plug in for a few minutes, you can get about one shave without the cord, if the unit was fully discharged.<br /><br />MOTOR<br />The motor is supposed to be one of the fastest on the market. It does operate well and it's relatively quiet compared with previous Braun shaver models. Braun designed it so that it also vibrates from side to side, essentially providing 4 cutting directions. In actuality, I do not think the side-to-side is very effective. I haven't changed my shaving stroke patterns and the time to complete my shave is always about the same (5 minutes).<br /><br />EXTERIOR<br />The exterior of the 8995 is a sleek satin look silver, and has a very smooth touch. Braun did away with a lot of the \\"grip pips\\" that were found on previous models, leaving only a few in certain key areas. I think this was a mistake. The shaver gripisn't quite as good as it used to be--if your hands are wet, you might very well drop the shaver. And that silver skin is delicate. Mine dropped into the sink and suffered an abrasion (just a cosmetic issue). You might notice that there is a new 5 series model out (the 590cc replaces the 8995) which features a very prominent side grip design--this is much better. But that model is quite a bit more expensive.<br /><br />CASE<br />I don't know if the 8995 comes with a case that holds only the shaver (no cord). My 8595 came with a hard plastic base and a flimsy plastic hinge that eventually broke off--useless. My old 7526 came with a faux leather pouch that holds the cord and shaver neatly. I don't know why Braun abandoned it (I now use it for my 8595).<br /><br />CLEANING SYSTEM<br />I find this device very ingenious, for a variety of reasons. First, it really does clean the shaver well. Second, it isn't overbearingly loud. And third, it has indicators to show when cleaning and charging are done. The fourth is revenue. Braun was very clever about this. If men are only going to spend money once every two years on the foil and cutter block, how could they make more money? Well, this cleaning system is the key. If the cleaner is used the way Braun recommends, you end up replacing the cleaning cartridge every month. The smart thing to do is buy the \\"value pack\\", which brings the cost down to about $5 per cartridge. How do you know when to change it? Well, the cleaning system will tell you. It detects when there is a high amount of particles in the solution, or if the solution is too low to flow through, and will flash the red cartridge light while simply not running until you replace the cartridge. The cleaner unit itself is slightly big (about 7\\" tall x 5\\" round), but smaller than its predecessor (which was 12\\" tall with a flimsy lock that would break). I don't recommend bringing the cleaner with you when traveling (but you don't really need to clean everyday anyway).<br /><br />But, I found a trick that Braun will probably shoot me for. I have been able to use a single cartridge for 1 full year before replacing. How did I do this? Well first of all, after each shave I dump my \\"whisker debris\\" down the sink, like you would normally do with the Flex Integral. It doesn't take long--simply pop off the foil, tap it in the sink, blow on both sides of the cutter block, replace the foil, and you're done in 10 seconds. This reduces the number of particles in the cleaning solution. So, why use the cleaning system at all, you may ask? It does do an excellent job of cleaning the cutter block, and whisker dust that is stuck on it and within the head and foil holder. A tedious task, even once or twice a week. When do I use the cleaning system? Well, usually whenever the shaver needs to be recharged. At this point, I take out the cartridge from my drawer, remove the top plugs, and slide it into the cleaner. Then I slide in the shaver and let the cleaner do its work. When the cleaning and charging is done, I remove the cleaning cartridge, reseal it with the plastic plugs, and put it away. This way the solution level does not get low from evaporation! Clever, eh? The only catch is that if you try to charge the shaver while mounted in the cleaner without the cartridge, it will not work. But you can always plug it in directly, without the cleaner. Anyway, that's my trick for getting around one this somewhat minor drawback. Some have said it's nice to have a \\"clean\\" shaver to use each time, but I find the cleaning process works well enough to use once per charge (just dump the whisker debris after each shave).<br /><br />COMPETITION<br />Braun's biggest competitor is Norelco, with their triple floating head system that has been their mainstay technology since the 1970's. And it's rather surprising that they haven't improved it all that much over the course of nearly 40 years. Although the motor tends to be quieter than Braun, the Norelco cutting action seems to fall a little long. Plus, the Norelco heads are more expensive to replace. But you have to give it to Norelco--the Arcitec design looks amazing, more sophisticated than Braun's old foil shaver design. And you can thoroughly rinse out the heads using water, so no bothersome cleaning base (and cleaning solution purchase) is needed.<br /><br />RECOMMENDATION<br />If price is no object, get the 8995. Otherwise, I recommend getting the 8985 or previous 8595 if you find it priced low enough. And don't forget the technique for extending the life of yourngle cartridge for 1 full year before replacing. How did I do this? Well first of all, after each shave I dump my \\"whisker debris\\" down the sink, like you would normally do with the Flex Integral. It doesn't take long--simply pop off the foil, tap it in the sink, blow on both sides of the cutter block, replace the foil, and you're done in 10 seconds. This reduces the number of particles in the cleaning solution. So, why use the cleaning system at all, you may ask? It does do an excellent job of cleaning the cutter block, and whisker dust that is stuck on it and within the head and foil holder. A tedious task, even once or twice a week. When do I use the cleaning system? Well, usually whenever the shaver needs to be recharged. At this point, I take out the cartridge from my drawer, remove the top plugs, and slide it into the cleaner. Then I slide in the shaver and let the cleaner do its work. When the cleaning and charging is done, I remove the cleaning cartridge, reseal it with the plastic plugs, and put it away. This way the solution level does not get low from evaporation! Clever, eh? The only catch is that if you try to charge the shaver while mounted in the cleaner without the cartridge, it will not work. But you can always plug it in directly, without the cleaner. Anyway, that's my trick for getting around one this somewhat minor drawback. Some have said it's nice to have a \\"clean\\" shaver to use each time, but I find the cleaning process works well enough to use once per charge (just dump the whisker debris after each shave).   7. Used Braun Flex Control (6550 model) for the past 6 years. Recently switched to Braun 8995 360 Complete. What a difference 6 years make in shaving technology! Best shaver that I have ever owned.   37. The Winner Is... The Panasonic ES8109S 3-blade - barely. Put the Remington blades and cutter (keeping the center blade of the Panasonic) on a Panasonic 13,000 RPM shaver and you would have the World's best electric shaver. The Remington shaved a little closer than the Panasonic and provided a faster shave. However, the difficulty in cleaning, noise and lack of a charging base tipped me to the Panasonic as the final choice. This is a review of three Panasonic models; ES8243A (4-blade), ES8109S (3-blade) and ES7109, the Remington MS2-390, the Norelco 8260 CC and the Braun Series 5 8995 (8985 & 8975 only differ in displays and cleaning). I have an average beard and have been using electric shavers (foils and rotaries) over 30 years. The models here are no better than any of the other higher quality shavers I've owned. It takes about 10 minutes (no shaver will give you a first-pass close shave) to get to that good dry shave (with or without pre-electric gels/oils) and you do have to put pressure on to get a close shave. This means recharging every 4-5 days. Gels/oils do make the process easier - not faster - and I have reviewed six of them on their Amazon sites. ES8109S: This 3-blade shaver gives a very close shave, with some work. It does give off a higher pitch `whine', while shaving, that is somewhat annoying, but is not what I would consider noisy. Nor is the cleaning operation noisy. Based upon other reviewers, I was expecting it to sound like a lawn mower, but it is just an occasional buzzing noise as it cleans. The \\"Arc Foil\\" design slows shaving (see discussion, below). ES8243A: I had hoped that the four blades of the Panasonic ES8243A just might be able to give a superior shave. As it turns out, the large four-blade surface is like trying to keep the end of a 2x4 on your face. It makes cutting in the areas where you don't have a lot of skin area (chin, jaw line, upper lip, base of sideburns, etc) more difficult. In fact, I think that the fourth blade in the middle actually interferes with a better shave and these two middle blades are not as good as the primary cutters. The \\"Arc Foil\\" design makes it even slower (see discussion, below). Another future problem with the 4-blade system is that you'll want to buy a new shaver when your blades and foil need to be replaced. What kind of an idiot is going to spend 80% of the cost of a new shaver just to get a set of new cutter blades and foil? All in all: the ES8243A 4-blade is a poor value. ES7109S: The flat design of the foil is a better design than the \\"Arc Foil\\" (see below). Unfortunately, this shaver has an under-powered motor and the floating head that cannot be locked. Panasonic discussion: Panasonic had developed an outstanding shaver line some ten years ago. My old ES8067 still shaves closer than this new \\"NANO Technology\\"- a misnomer (marketing gimmick). I think the reason is that Panasonic's older models came with cutting blades with the individual blades having been about half the width of all of Panasonic's newer cutting blades (including replacements). This means more surface area on the newer blades and that means less cutting. Remington has the ideal blades (that Panasonic used to make) and it shows in closer cutting and less time spent doing so. Additionally, these new Panasonic \\"Arc Foil\\" shavers have the foil curving AWAY from your face at the ends of the foil, further decreasing exposure to the blades and requiring many more passes to cover the same area. Unfortunately, Panasonic puts their better motor (13,000 RPMs) only on these ill-conceived \\"Arc Foil\\" designs. Battery time on the Panasonics is the shortest of all shavers reviewed here. The Panasonic trimmers are so narrow, on all of these models, that you will not be able to trim sideburns with one attempt. You will have to re-position the trimmer to get what you missed. This increases the probability that you will get an uneven sideburn. The Remington MS2-390 has the blades that thePanasonics should have (and did have years ago): flat foil area (not \\"Arc Foiled\\"), good length (25% longer) and ultra thin cutting blades. As a result, closeness of the shave is better and time spent is shorter. This is, however, the loudest (and it is loud) of all shavers and there are no bells and whistles. Using a pre-shave oil/gel will gum up the blades, as with any shaver, but these blades pop off with even the slightest brushing so be prepared to watch them fall into the sink with every cleaning attempt. A charging stand would greatly increase the convenience of this shaver. Remington did a poor job with the details. The Braun Series 5 8995 tries hard (you can hear noticeable slowing when necessary pressure is applied, like a lawn mower when it reaches thicker grass), but it doesn't get quite as close as the Panasonics or Remington without leaving a stronger burning sensation after the shave. The Braun can also leave burn marks and even cuts (nose and lips) that will bleed. Odd: you would think that, with it getting so close as to actually burn the skin, it would also give a closer shave. I suppose this is proof that shavers cannot \\"lift\\" hairs to cut better. Additionally, the design of the handle is inferior, making positioning more difficult. It does have a much wider trimmer and longer battery life between charges, though. The Norelco 8260 CC: I used this rotary-type of shaver for many years during the 80's. I switched to foil and found I could get a closer shave. This is still the case. Additionally, because of the circular blades, it is somewhat difficult to target certain spots for cleanup. However, this is the quietest shaver. PS: don't accept the nonsense about giving your face 30 days to adjust, unless you are coming off a blade. If you are accustomed to an electric shaver, you only need a week or two to determine the difference. The only thing magical about 30 days is that you can no longer return it for a refund - what a coincidence!
  38. If you're going to buy this, that's good because it does give a quick shave. It shaves very fast, but that's only the good news. The bad news is that it irritates my skin beyond belief, and it gives a poor shave. Not close at all, I give up I'm gonna throw this thing away.

  43. I purchased this shaver several years ago. For the first year or so I liked it a lot. I agree with most of the pros/cons of the other reviews, in brief, pro: close even shave, long battery life, cleaning stand is handy, can use corded or cordless, can clean manually; con: cleaning cycle is long and loud, shaver is loud (not so much at first, but more on this later). But there are some downsides that you don't see in the reviews. * I get maybe 4-5 months of use out of a head. Some original reviews said they'd last a year. New heads cost a fair amount. * The cleaning refills aren't cheap. They last only about a month at best, and shipping costs are significant w.r.t the overall price of a package of three. * The floating heads tend to come apart. They're held in place by two black plastic pieces that fit on either side of the head. After a month of use or so, these tend to come off when the head is released. They aren't so easy to fit back in, and tend to keep loosening. It becomes difficult to either cleanly release the head, or snap it fully back in. And the main thing is, the older the razor gets, the shorter the life of the cleaning heads. They don't fit as securely, and they tend to jam, and they start snagging on your beard or stalling, so you have to go really easy in order to ensure they keep cutting. So the overall life of the shaver doesn't seem so great. The end result is I pretty much have to replace this shaver after about three years. My previous shaver I had for over ten years, and while it didn't shave as well initially, it shaved decently all of its life. Basically I only replaced it because the rotary heads were getting more and more difficult to find. These are things you don't appreciate until after a year or so of use. The reviews I had read before buying the shaver were from people who'd had the shaver a few weeks, and were pretty effusive. And I liked it too, when I first got it. But you need to keep in mind whenreading the reviews that by and large, these are people who've been using an old shaver who are now using a new one. So I can't really recommend this shaver.

  78. The first thing to know about ANY electric shaver is that you really need to give your face about two weeks of daily shaving with only the electric to truly get a good idea of the performance of the device. The second is that it probably won't shave as close as a blade, despite any advertising the manufacturer might put out there. That said, THIS one will probably give a closer shave than any electric on the market. I have used primarily electric shavers for about 35 years, and I've run the gamut from the basic Remington, to the new-fangled (for its day) Schick Flexamatic with its first-of-its-kind foil screen head, to the triple head Norelco. I replaced the Norelco about 9 years ago with a top rated Braun, liking what I read in the reviews, and what I saw when I looked at it in the stores, and was very pleased with its performance, as it gave me the closest electric shave I had ever experienced. Mind you, no electric will give you the baby's-butt-smooth closness that you would experience with a Gilette blade and Edge Gel, (my personal closeness benchmark) but that puppy came damn close! So when it started to die after a long and faithful life, there was no question in my mind that another Braun was in my future. The only question was which. Not much thought went into that decision, as I figured why not get the top-of-the-line model with the auto-cleaning feature. Although it is rather pricy when compared to other brands of electrics out there, believe me, you get what you pay for. Right out of the box (after a quick charge) the 8995 worked flawlessly, and I was a bit surprised to note that even though I had been using a Braun for years, it still took several days for my beard to get set up to the new foil head technology on this model. Once my personal break-in was over, I was blown away to find that this latest model was even better than my venerable 9 year old Braun which I had held in such high esteem. Even the tricky spots under the lower lip and at the base of the neck (where the hairs seem to grow in whatever direction they damn well feel like and even that seems to change on a daily basis)were no match for the contortionist-like head of the Braun, and the pop-up trimmer made short (no pun intended) work of the sideburn/mustache trimming tasks. As far as the cleaning/charging base goes, this is one of the more interesting features. The shaver goes in upside down - in one piece, nothing to disassemble - on roughly a 30 degree angle, and an automatic cycle analyzes the cleanliness of the shaver. (though I have my theory that it pretty much assumes the level of cleanliness based on how long the shaver has been used since the last cleaning/charging cycle and determines a commensurate cleaning accordingly) Then, using an alcohol based cleaning solution in a replaceable cartridge, (the shaver comes with one - they say it lasts about 30 cleanings, and the cleaning/charging base LED will let you know when it's circling the drain) it flushes and cleans the shaver head, and then automatically dries it, in a total time of about an hour. While this is happening the shaver is also charged, too. It comes out in a like new state of clean, with a pleasant lemon scent to boot. And after cleaning, the first shave seems smoother, as if the cleaning solution left a lubricant on the foil. Braun claims no memory effect on the shaver's battery, so theoretically, you could charge and clean daily. Not a bad idea, especially for those with heavy daily beard growth. And if you're on the road, you can still clean it manually with the included brush, and refresh the battery by plugging the charging cord into the bottom of the shaver. Mercedes, BMW, Porsche, Braun. German engineering. Guys, need I say more?

A couple days later I called and they said call back in a week, they still hadn't received them. The shortage (and perhaps the problem) may be due to the fact that the power supplies are supposed to automatically adjust between American and European voltage levels when necessary. Update 10/02/07: I was called late last week and told they had the power supplies in stock. Picked one up today. I have not used it and according to the sticker that was on the razor when it arrives it takes approximately two weeks for one's beard to adjust to an electric razor. Update 11/13/07: After using this razor for over a month now I have to say I am quite happy with it. I bought this product because I hate to shave. I have a thick, fast-growing beard and shaving takes a long time, even if I do it every day. And, I have to change blades every week or so, which gets expensive. So, I wanted something fast and easy that cut back on the blade purchases and not give the nicks and cuts of everyday shaving. So, the obvious answer would be to turn to an electric razor, right? Right, except that very electric razor I used in the past did a miserable job, especially around the neck. I happened to read some great reviews for this product and decided to give it a try. (Leaving aside the ridiculous amount of time I spent trying to get it repaired) I could not be happier with the results. The shave is quick and easy and I have had no problems with reactions after shaving. The shave on my cheeks is darn close to razor smooth but the 5 'o clock shadow does pop up a bit early. The goatee area is a little less smooth but still good and the razor holds a good charge and comes with a carrying case so it could be toted around for a pre-meeting cleanup or what have you. As for the neck, I have been pleasantly surprised. For everyday use I have had no problems with shaving the neck, but when I take a couple days off, like on a weekend, there are the couple stray hairs that it can't seem to cut and I ultimately have to touch razor to skin, albeit briefly. The cleaning base is passably quick but I suggest you do the cleaning after your shaves so you don't have to wait around. You may not have to clean it after every shave but I recommend doing it somewhat often as it noticeably affects the quality of the shave (at least with my thick hair). Final conclusion: For the product itself I give it *****/***** (5 out of 5). It is the most I could have asked from an electric razor. The situation with the power supply is probably just an unfortunate anomaly and chances are your razor won't have this issue. Be warned however that if it does the product cannot be returned to amazon due to the flammable cleaning solution and you will most likely have to deal with an independent repair facility, assuming there is even one near by. With this in mind, I have decided to keep the official rating at 1 star, so that people wondering about a possible down side to the purchase can check the one star reviews and read this. (I do this expressly with the knowledge that my one vote will not effect the good overall rating of this item.)

I used to use my Panasonic shaver all over the places, in front of my computer, sometimes if I'm late for work or events, I shave while I drive (I know I'm not supposed to do this, as it's dangerous, but I do it sometimes), but I can't do it anymore with this Braun shaver. - this shaver is LOUD and VIBRATES BIG TIME ... I really mean it ... - cleaning solution didn't last more than 3 weeks as I use it once everyday, the box says it's supposed to last for 30 days. - cleaning fluid is expensive - oh well, if you want auto-cleaning, you gotta pay for it. - dried cleaning fluid stays on the shaver, which eventually stays on your face after you shave, and it tastes bad, bitter, and nasty. - moving over from a rotary shaver, this shaver gave me a lot of razor burns, but after about 2 weeks of constant usage, I'm gettingless and less razor burns. - can't shave under running water, therefore unable to shave while in shower. CONCLUSION: I'm not very satisfied with this system, and I don't think this shaver does the price-tag any justice, as it had way more cons, than pros. I'm returning this shaver and buying the top of the line Panasonic electric shaver.

  195. I purchased this razor to replace a Braun 7540. This is my third Braun. I had a low end Remington before that. I like the Brauns because they are good quality, provide a good shave, have long battery life, and pack smaller than the three-headed rotary razors. I have never tried the better quality razors from other makers so cannot make a direct comparison. The Braun 7540 was a great razor. I had it for at least 6 years and only replaced it because the battery or motor was beginning to wear down. I read many reviews of the Braun higher end razors and a few competitors, and chose the 8995 for several reasons. First, I was happy with my first two Brauns. Second, it had strong reviews overall. Third, it packs smaller than other brands. And I can afford the more expensive razor even though I don't NEED the fancy display and self-cleaning system. I was sceptical of the cleaning system, including cost of cleaner cartridges, but decided to give it a try. When the razor first arrived, I was a bit concerned about its build quality. As I read in a couple reviews, it seemed a bit more plastic than I expected for the money. Then I compared it to my old razor that I was happy with and decided it was good to go. My one concern is the lock mechanism. I am interested to see how long it lasts (my 7540 lock broke about 3 years ago; the razor still works, but I had to pull out the button and spring for the razor to work). The razor works great. It cuts closer and faster than my 7540, cutting my shave time down about 1/3. I have to reshave my tough spots less times with this razor. I did get minor razor burn (nothing visible) the first couple times I used it, but I quickly adjusted. The cleaning system is nifty. I don't use it every day because I don't think it is necessary and because it is actually a bit noisy and may disturb my wife. I use it once or twice a week and it works great. The cleaning time can be up to an hour, and it turns the razor on periodically, thus the noise. The base still tells me the washing fluid is full, so I cannot comment on how long the cleaning fluid will last. I've had the razor for over a month. Some have commented that the cleaning fluid evaporates even if you don't use it, but I haven't noticed this. If I do, I will remove the cartridge between cleanings and put the cap back on. Braun does need to sell the cleaning fluid in bulk containers allowing us to refill the cartridges ourselves and reducing the amount of waste. Overall, excellent razor. Build quality feel is about 90% as good as my old 7540, but that is subjective. Shaves great (average beard thickness, some tough to get hair on my neck). 3 year 6 month update: The razor is still functioning great. I have noticed some deterioration in the battery, but this could be because I don't store it in the charger so the battery gets cycled to near empty regularly. I don't have the counterspace to keep it charging. Still, I go over a week or two without having to charge it. I have not yet replaced the blade/screen yet and it still shaves well. Also, I only clean it once or twice per month. In between, I tap it in the sink and blow out the shavings every couple shaves. The cleaning system is still working fine. In order to keep the cleaning fluid from evaporating, I remove it from the base and put the cap back on. It only takes a minute to do, and I've saved a small fortune (likely a hundred or two dollars over three years) by doing this. When the battery gets low, the digital screen will give you minutes of shave time remaining. It seems accurate - though I've never actually clocked it - a very handy feature. Overall, still 5 stars. Very happy with the razor.

Moreover, the major manufacturers (Braun, Panasonic and Norelco) are constantly upgrading their products, and it is difficult to know if the upgrades are gimmicks (and justifications for higher prices) or real improvements. Therefore, the selection of an electric shaver is largely trial and error, and comparison shopping is a must. So after one shave and putting it back in the charger it said it just needed an \\"eco\\" clean. If I would shave, then clean it manually, then not put it back in the base and shave again, and clean it manually again, then put it in the base it said it needed a \\"normal\\" clean. So it's not based on how dirty it is, it's based on how long it's used between cleans. So it's probably better to just let it clean itself using the \\"eco\\" clean after every shave, because I think three \\"eco\\" cleanings is less time than an \\"intensive\\" one, meaning less cleaning solution used. After 2 months and 35 shaves; According to the base, the cleaning solution is still full, so I'm happy with that. But the other day the display on the shaver said to replace foil and cutting head, I only saw it once, but I was hoping that would last for at least 6 months, we'll see..

  222. I've had the opportunity to use this shaver over nearly a month, now; my first electric razor. I can't find any reason for wanting to replace this it any time soon. Before purchasing, I considered many other models, including other lower-end Braun series, Philips, and higher end Norelco and Remington models. From what I gathered, I considered the Braun brand to be top of the line. Buy it if you can afford it.<br /><br />Form<br />The 360 is rather aesthetically pleasing. The commercials last year were awesome, as it displayed an electric razor that literally washes itself when placed on its charger. The footprint of the charger itself is relatively large - nearly 5\\" in diameter - it will fit nicely on a sink with a long countertop. Every shave leaves a light citrus scent. Although it weights a bit more than the average electric razor, it is still fairly light. It fits well in averaged-sized hands, and when you turn it on, the sound, the feel, and the quality: it instills the confidence knowing that it will leave a fresh, close shave.<br /><br />Function<br />One of the first things that stand out is an LCD screen that frequently informs one of the battery levels and its 'thought processes.' Although I do not feel that it is a necessary feature, it's nice. When turned on, the razor is loud and smooth enough to let you know it will cut. When it goes about your face, you need to run it at different angles in order to get all the hairs. It does well when the hair is less than 3 mm; longer, and the trim feature (which works well with sideburns) should be used prior to getting a close shave. The neck of the razor bends up and down to fit the angles of the shave; the blade end is a bit stiff; however, the metal itself does not flex to the contours of the skin, but still manages to get everything. The closeness can be compared to razor blade quality. It is that close. The advantages include very little chance at nicks, and no need to carry shaving cream. The cleaning feature works well: after you put the razor back in the charger it assesses how dirty the razor is, and adjusts its cleaning settings accordingly. After you hit the clean button, it goes to work, taking approximately 30 to 50 minutes to clean. If you don't press the clean button and let the razor sit for a few days, the charger will update to a brisker cleaning setting, as it will take note the increased amount of debris collected along the razor. It also knows not to clean if you've just removed the razor, turned on, but not used it, and then replaced it. One can charge the 360 directly, if they must travel, instead of hauling the entire charger. The batteries last quite a while uncharged, and for a week's trip, the power chord is not necessary.<br /><br />Form and function were difficult to separate in this razor, because the two were so closely tied together. You need give your skin a few weeks to get used to the electric razor, also. The first shaves feel very close. Often, you need to pull your skin so that the razor can reach everything. My only concerns were replacing the cleaning fluid. It's been a month and the chamber is still full of fluid, but I wonder how often it will need replacing. I recommend this razor if one intends on switching from a razor blade-equipped razor.<br /><br />UPDATE (4/08/2010):<br />I've had this electric razor for more than 2.5 years, now. Since then, my opinions about it have not changed. I've replaced the blades as recommended, however I have noted that they were still very sharp when I took them out. I've also noticed that I can make the cleaning solution last longer if I shaved every day to prevent long hairs from accumulating along the blades and in the solution. As a result, hairs don't collect as quickly under the foil and the solution remains cleaner, longer. This last bottle of solution is \\"half full\\" at even two months, amazing. ***One important issue I need to point out, however, is that I'vehad to replace the charger once. The problem here was that the connecting points between the charger/cleaner oxidized as time passed, so after a year, the charger no longer recognized the razor. I replaced the piece, and have had no other issues since.*** On a final note, I recommend buying the cleaning solution straight from Amazon's website. Amazon has the option of subscribing to a service where the solution is automatically sent (at a discounted rate) every few months (as you decide). Not a bad deal, since it costs less on Amazon than at a store, for me.blem here was that the connecting points between the charger/cleaner oxidized as time passed, so after a year, the charger no longer recognized the razor. Not a bad deal, since it costs less on Amazon than at a store, for me.

They worked but I tired of hot sticky lather on my face everyday after showering. I never really got them to shave my neck well unless I re-lathered and that was too time consuming. If you do shave like this though, use a lather heater. You will be glad you did. I can get a fair amount of ingrown hairs on the sides of my face, usually they do not get too inflamed or go very deep but they seem less numerous with the Braun. I have fine curly/wavy blond hair that seems to want to get near the surface and then go sideways. I have ended this problem by using 1 crushed UNCOATED aspirin in 1 oz. of water and dabbing it on with my fingers after exfoliating with a bath cloth and after I have finished shaving. Braun usage info: You will likely need a few weeks to get used to it. Use it with a clean, dry face (at least 30 minutes after showering) or you will bring out the \\"intensive cleaning needed\\" message. Never try and blow matter from the cutter block for the same reason. When refill gets closer to running out, let razor dry out after cleaning then pop foil off a look for nagging droplets. Blow them out from the inside to the outside. They can trigger the 'intense cleaning' warning if not removed. I pop and \\"buzz\\" the cutter/foil after use and clean it using base every other day (24 hours clock time) an and usually it always comes up \\"economy\\" cleaning (I suspect it will become \\"normal\\" after 36 hours.) The cleaning stand does work well but I don't leave it plugged in all the time. I am covering it in a plastic grocery bag (closed and draped around base with the handles tucked under the cord stub protruding from base) to slow evaporation of the solution. Higher room temperature will in IMO be the biggest factor in how long it lasts, though some is 'cooked off' the razor in the cleaning process. Refills in cooler months can last up to 10 more uses than refills used in warmer months. Lowest is 29 uses and highest is 39 so far. I tried using to clean razor for a week or two without the base using brush and manually oiling it. The Braun is better with the alcohol. It irritated my skin somewhat to use oil or becuase it was not cleaned by alcohol and the razor did not shave as close. Clippercide (I do not know its active ingredient) or Remington's Shaver Saver silicone based spray might work. I think the shave counter is annoying in that it should only count shaves of 2 minutes or more as shaves. I often shave for 2-3 minutes, wash my face, dry it a few minutes and then shave any spots I left half finished which only takes 30 seconds but counts as another shave on the master counter. I have had no issue with making holes in the foil. I try not to press it too hard against my face.

  296. I've used the Braun 8595 electric shaver for three years. To my mind it has serious deficiencies.After three years of use (well past the suggested break-in period) I've found the following: *There are some areas of the face that it absolutely refuses to shave...some longer hairs on the right cheek, under-the-chin hairs on the left side, under the chin centre, and the neck. For these I use the Schick Body Groomer, and that works well. The Braun cannot be made to deal with these areas no matter what I try. This is a very serious deficiency. Changing the head position from free to locked makes some difference, but it will still not deal with the problem areas I mentioned. *Like so many other electrics, you will not get a close shave with just one pass. You will either have to press very hard (something Braun, recognizing its own deficiencies, suggests and which does not work) or go over and over the same area using one's hand to make the bristles stand up. Even then, this procedure is ineffective with certain areas. *Like other electrics which simply lop off the top of the hair, shaves with this shaver do not last. Expect to shave at least twice a day if you have a beloved. I do believe that the inability of this shaver to cover all parts of the face without using an additional grooming aid is a serious deficiency of this and of all electric shavers, which use the same procedure. A razor blade cuts off hairs at the base. It does not nibble at them as an electric does. A shaver cannot cut below the skin line: a razor can. What should be sold is not one shaver but rather a combination of shavers that would do all the jobs required.However, to do so would be to admit the failure of the principal shaver, which is where the big bucks lie. I recommend buying the cheapest shaver in the line plus a Schick Body Groomer (which is a great idea, anyway!). The cheaper shaver will probably do as good a job as the expensive models with all their technological and useless doo-dads, which is what you are paying your $$$$ for.

And it really irritated the skin on my neck and chin. After two weeks of using the Bruan, the awkwardness started to go away and the irritation on my skin began to disappear. The shave may have been marginally better than I got with my Norelco. But it wasn't good enough to make be that much happier with the Braun. The Braun's cleaning system was driving me crazy. The shaver seems to need cleaning about every fourth shave, and I can't get over the feeling that the cleaning system is just a way for Braun to make money on consumable cleaning fluid. I resent having this big cleaning unit sitting on my bathroom counter, where space is at a premium. My dissatisfaction with the Braun sent me back into research mode. I've taken up wet shaving again, starting with a double-edge blade and some luxurious shaving products from the Art of Shaving. Wet shaving with these products is so vastly superior to the performance of any electric, that the ritual of wet shaving has become an unexpected pleasure. I've gone back to using a double-edge safety razer and liked it so much I just ordered a straight razor and a strop. This setup will cost no more than the Braun, and its vastly superior in results. Guys, it might be worthwhile to consider dumping electrics altogether and going back to wet shaving. If you've hated wet shaving before, maybe you'd benefit by using the Web to research all the resources for learning how to do it right. Inow keep my Braun electric for travel, and I find I can't wait to get home for a good, close shave with my razor.
  326. Well, after many years of trying to find the perfect electronic shaver I think I've found it. It even takes care of those pesky whiskers on my neck that other shavers were never able to cut. Even after several days of not shaving the Braun has no problem giving me a great, smooth shave. In addition to the awesome shave the clean up procedure is great - just stick it in the docking station and voila! - it's like new every time I use it. While some might consider it a bit expensive (I did) it's well worth the money I paid for it.
